Second Proof: Infinite Parts and the Impossibility of Traversal
Second proof that infinite parts make traversal impossible in finite time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second rational proof for the finitude of parts: that an infinite number of parts would make traversing any finite distance impossible within a finite time.

Core Idea
An infinite series of halves cannot be completed in finite time.

This lesson presents the second proof against infinite parts, based on motion across a distance. Imagine a mover heading toward a goal. To reach it, they must first cover half the distance, then half the remainder, and so on. If the parts are infinite, this series never ends, making the journey impossible in finite time. The passage formalizes this argument and shows how it ties distance, motion, and time together.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Notice the logical flow of the argument.
The passage uses technical terms like 'متحرك' (mover) and 'غاية' (goal).
2
Understand the halving argument
Focus on the first part: to reach the goal, the mover must traverse half the distance, then half of the remainder, and so on infinitely. Ask yourself why this cannot be done in finite time.
This is a classic 'dichotomy paradox' similar to Zeno's.
3
Trace the extension to motion and time
The passage then states that infinite parts of distance imply infinite parts of motion (since motion corresponds to distance), and that in turn implies infinite parts of time. This reinforces the impossibility.
This shows the interconnectedness of distance, motion, and time in the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: أن لا تناهي الأجزاء يستلزم امتناع وصول المتحرك إلى غاية ما في المسافة لتوقفه على قطع نصفها ونصف نصفها ، وهلم جرا إلى ما لا يتناهى وذلك لا يتصور فيما يتناهى من الزمان، وقد يعبر عن هذا الوجه بأنه يلزم امتناع قطع المسافة المعينة في زمان متناه، وتقرر بأن عدم تناهي أجزاء المسافة يستلزم عدم تناهي أجزاء الحركة المنطبقة عليها وهو يستلزم عدم تناهي أجزاء الزمان المنطبق على الحركة .
The second: That the infinite [number] of parts entails the impossibility of the mover's reaching any goal in the distance, because it depends on cutting half of it and half of that half, and so on ad infinitum, and that is inconceivable within finite time. This aspect is sometimes expressed as that the impossibility of traversing a given distance in finite time is necessary, and it is established that the infinite parts of the distance entail infinite parts of motion corresponding to it, which entails infinite parts of time corresponding to the motion.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for the finitude of parts, based on the impossibility of traversing an infinite number of parts in a finite time. The argument is that if a distance has infinitely many parts, then to reach the end, the mover must first traverse half the distance, then half of the remainder, and so on infinitely. This sequence cannot be completed in a finite time. The same point is expressed as: infinite parts of distance imply infinite parts of motion (since motion corresponds to the distance traversed), and this in turn implies infinite parts of time (since time corresponds to motion). Thus, traversing any finite distance in finite time would be impossible if the distance had infinite parts.

Key Terms
متحرك (mover)
غاية (goal)
مسافة (distance)
حركة (motion)
زمان (time)
قطع (traversal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think this argument is about actual infinite division (like Zeno's paradox being unsolvable).
Correction: The argument is about potential infinite division: the process of halving can be repeated indefinitely, but that does not mean the distance is actually composed of infinitely many parts. The proof shows that if the parts were actually infinite, traversal would be impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, why can a mover not reach the end of a distance if the parts are infinite?
A) Because the mover gets tired
B) Because it would need to cover an infinite number of halves, which is impossible in finite time
C) Because the distance is too long
D) Because the mover's speed is insufficient

Key Takeaway
The second proof shows that infinite parts would make finite motion impossible, thus parts must be finite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You perform countless movements every day without thinking. This lesson argues that such motion is only possible because the world is built on finite parts—each half, each step, each action has a limit. If you truly believe that, does it change how you see the simplest act of standing up? What can you do today to thank Allah for the very structure that makes motion possible?
?
The proof shows that infinite halves would trap you forever—you would never reach any goal. Reflect on your spiritual goals: are there 'infinite halves' in your life, such as endless excuses or procrastination, that prevent you from reaching closeness to Allah? What is the first finite step you can take right now to break that chain?
?
This passage challenges the idea that infinite parts can be traversed. Consider the concept of 'finitude'—your existence, your time, your abilities are all finite. How does accepting this finitude free you from the stress of trying to do everything? What one finite commitment can you make today that will have enduring value?

First Proof: Boundedness Implies Finitude
First proof: boundedness implies finitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first argument for the finitude of body parts: that being bounded between two boundaries entails finitude.

Core Idea
Whatever is bounded between two endpoints is necessarily finite.

The first proof given by the proponents of atomism is elegantly simple: anything confined between two limits—whether number or magnitude—cannot be infinite. This principle is foundational to their rejection of infinite divisibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note that it states the first proof directly.
The proof is concise: boundedness implies finitude.
2
Identify the key claim
The claim is that parts of the body are bounded by its extremes, and anything bounded is finite.
This applies to both numbers and magnitudes.
3
Reflect on the logic
Consider why boundedness entails finitude. This is a self-evident rational judgment.
If something had no boundary, it could be infinite, but here boundaries are present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احتج القائلون بالجزء على أن أجزاء الجسم متناهية نفياً لقول النظام لوجوه : الأول: أنها محصورة بين حاصرين فكل ما هو كذلك عدداً كان أو مقداراً فهو متناه بالضرورة.
الثاني: أن لا تناهي الأجزاء يستلزم امتناع وصول المتحرك إلى غاية ما في المسافة لتوقفه على قطع نصفها ونصف نصفها ، وهلم جرا إلى ما لا يتناهى وذلك لا يتصور فيما يتناهى من الزمان، وقد يعبر عن هذا الوجه بأنه يلزم امتناع قطع المسافة المعينة في زمان متناه، وتقرر بأن عدم تناهي أجزاء المسافة يستلزم عدم تناهي أجزاء الحركة المنطبقة عليها وهو يستلزم عدم تناهي أجزاء الزمان المنطبق على الحركة .
الثالث : أنه يستلزم امتناع لحوق السريع بالبطيء إذ ابتداء الحركة بعده لأنه إذا قطع جزءاً فالبطيء أيضاً. قطع جزءاً إذ لا أقل منه ضرورة، ولا تخلل للسكنات بشهادة الخس والبرهان، وإنما اعتبر البطيء دون الواقف مع أنه كذلك لأنه حينئذ يكون ذكر السرعة لغواً، ويصير هذا بعينه طريق امتناع قطع المتحرك مسافة ما، ووصوله إلى غاية ما، ولا يخفى أن هذا الوجه جار فيما إذا كانت الأجزاء متناهية، وأن الوجوه الثلاثة إنما تنتهض على من يقول بلا تناهي الأجزاء في كل امتداد يفرض في الجسم ، وفيما بين كل طرفين من أطرافه، وجهتين من جهاته، وأما على القول بلا تناهيها في مجموع الامتدادات وفيما بين جميع الأطراف والجهات فلا إلا بين تناهي عدد الامتدادات .
The proponents of the atom argued that the parts of the body are finite, rejecting the statement of al-Nazzam, through proofs: First: They are bounded between two boundaries, and everything that is so, whether number or magnitude, is necessarily finite. Second: That the infinity of parts entails the impossibility of the moving object reaching any limit in distance, because it is dependent on crossing its half, and half of its half, and so on ad infinitum, and that is inconceivable in a finite time. This argument is expressed as the impossibility of traversing a given distance in a finite time. It is established that the infinity of the parts of the distance entails the infinity of the parts of motion that correspond to it, and that entails the infinity of the parts of time that correspond to the motion. Third: That it entails the impossibility of the swift overtaking the slow, since [the swift] begins motion after it [the slow] because when it covers a part, the slow also covers a part, since there is no smaller part necessarily, and there is no intervening rest, attested by sense and proof. The slow is considered rather than the stationary, although the same applies, because then mentioning speed would be pointless. This becomes the very means of preventing the moving object from traversing a distance and reaching a limit. It is not hidden that this point applies when the parts are finite, and that the three arguments are effective only against one who claims the infinity of parts in every extension supposed in the body, and between every two of its extremities, and in two of its directions. But on the view of their infinity in the totality of extensions and between all extremities and directions, [the objection does not apply] except [by] the finitude of the number of extensions.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents three distinct proofs offered by the proponents of the atom (al-qāʾilūn bi al-juzʾ) to establish that the parts of a body are finite, thereby refuting the position of al-Nazzām who held that bodies are composed of infinite parts. The first proof (al-awwal) argues that the parts of a body are bounded by the two extremes of the body, and anything bounded between two boundaries—whether in number or magnitude—is necessarily finite. The second proof (al-thānī) argues that if parts are infinite, then a moving body could never reach its destination, because to traverse any distance it must first cross half of it, then half of the remaining half, ad infinitum; thus the motion could never be completed in a finite time. The proof extends to show that infinite parts of distance would require infinite parts of motion and infinite parts of time. The third proof (al-thālith) argues that if parts are infinite, a swift object could never overtake a slow one, because when the swift covers a part, the slow also covers a part (since there is no smallest part and no intervening rest). The slow is considered instead of the stationary object to avoid making speed irrelevant. The passage then clarifies that these three proofs are directed only against the claim that parts are infinite in every supposed extension and between every two extremities. If the opponent claims infinity only in the totality of extensions, then the proofs do not apply except by reductio on the finitude of the number of extensions.

Key Terms
جزء
تناهي
محصور بين حاصرين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what makes the parts of a body finite?
A) They are created by God.
B) They are bounded between two boundaries.
C) They are indivisible.
D) They are small.

Key Takeaway
The first proof is that boundedness between two ends necessarily entails finitude.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your life, your abilities, your knowledge are all bounded. Does this reality cause you to turn to the Unbounded One in humility and need, or do you still live as though you have no end?
?
The proof here is clear and self-evident, yet many people ignore it. In what specific area of your life are you ignoring a clear truth because it is inconvenient? What will you do about it?
?
If you accept that everything bounded is finite, and that only God is infinite, how does this change the way you prioritize your time, possessions, and relationships? Are you living as though finite things can give infinite satisfaction?

Second Proof: Impossibility of Traversing Distance
Second proof: infinite parts prevent crossing distance in finite time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how infinite parts would make motion impossible in finite time, as argued in the second proof.

Core Idea
Infinite halves prevent reaching any goal in finite time.

The second proof uses the famous dichotomy paradox: if distance is infinitely divisible, one can never cross half, then half of half, ad infinitum, making motion impossible in finite time. This argument ties together distance, motion, and time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the logical chain of the argument.
The argument is more elaborate than the first.
2
Understand the chain
The proof links infinite parts of distance to infinite parts of motion, and then to infinite parts of time.
Each step is a conditional entailment.
3
See the contradiction
If time is finite, infinite parts of time cannot exist. Thus, infinite parts of distance are impossible.
This refutes infinite divisibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احتج القائلون بالجزء على أن أجزاء الجسم متناهية نفياً لقول النظام لوجوه : الأول: أنها محصورة بين حاصرين فكل ما هو كذلك عدداً كان أو مقداراً فهو متناه بالضرورة.
الثاني: أن لا تناهي الأجزاء يستلزم امتناع وصول المتحرك إلى غاية ما في المسافة لتوقفه على قطع نصفها ونصف نصفها ، وهلم جرا إلى ما لا يتناهى وذلك لا يتصور فيما يتناهى من الزمان، وقد يعبر عن هذا الوجه بأنه يلزم امتناع قطع المسافة المعينة في زمان متناه، وتقرر بأن عدم تناهي أجزاء المسافة يستلزم عدم تناهي أجزاء الحركة المنطبقة عليها وهو يستلزم عدم تناهي أجزاء الزمان المنطبق على الحركة .
الثالث : أنه يستلزم امتناع لحوق السريع بالبطيء إذ ابتداء الحركة بعده لأنه إذا قطع جزءاً فالبطيء أيضاً. قطع جزءاً إذ لا أقل منه ضرورة، ولا تخلل للسكنات بشهادة الخس والبرهان، وإنما اعتبر البطيء دون الواقف مع أنه كذلك لأنه حينئذ يكون ذكر السرعة لغواً، ويصير هذا بعينه طريق امتناع قطع المتحرك مسافة ما، ووصوله إلى غاية ما، ولا يخفى أن هذا الوجه جار فيما إذا كانت الأجزاء متناهية، وأن الوجوه الثلاثة إنما تنتهض على من يقول بلا تناهي الأجزاء في كل امتداد يفرض في الجسم ، وفيما بين كل طرفين من أطرافه، وجهتين من جهاته، وأما على القول بلا تناهيها في مجموع الامتدادات وفيما بين جميع الأطراف والجهات فلا إلا بين تناهي عدد الامتدادات .
The proponents of the atom argued that the parts of the body are finite, rejecting the statement of al-Nazzam, through proofs: First: They are bounded between two boundaries, and everything that is so, whether number or magnitude, is necessarily finite. Second: That the infinity of parts entails the impossibility of the moving object reaching any limit in distance, because it is dependent on crossing its half, and half of its half, and so on ad infinitum, and that is inconceivable in a finite time. This argument is expressed as the impossibility of traversing a given distance in a finite time. It is established that the infinity of the parts of the distance entails the infinity of the parts of motion that correspond to it, and that entails the infinity of the parts of time that correspond to the motion. Third: That it entails the impossibility of the swift overtaking the slow, since [the swift] begins motion after it [the slow] because when it covers a part, the slow also covers a part, since there is no smaller part necessarily, and there is no intervening rest, attested by sense and proof. The slow is considered rather than the stationary, although the same applies, because then mentioning speed would be pointless. This becomes the very means of preventing the moving object from traversing a distance and reaching a limit. It is not hidden that this point applies when the parts are finite, and that the three arguments are effective only against one who claims the infinity of parts in every extension supposed in the body, and between every two of its extremities, and in two of its directions. But on the view of their infinity in the totality of extensions and between all extremities and directions, [the objection does not apply] except [by] the finitude of the number of extensions.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents three distinct proofs offered by the proponents of the atom (al-qāʾilūn bi al-juzʾ) to establish that the parts of a body are finite, thereby refuting the position of al-Nazzām who held that bodies are composed of infinite parts. The first proof (al-awwal) argues that the parts of a body are bounded by the two extremes of the body, and anything bounded between two boundaries—whether in number or magnitude—is necessarily finite. The second proof (al-thānī) argues that if parts are infinite, then a moving body could never reach its destination, because to traverse any distance it must first cross half of it, then half of the remaining half, ad infinitum; thus the motion could never be completed in a finite time. The proof extends to show that infinite parts of distance would require infinite parts of motion and infinite parts of time. The third proof (al-thālith) argues that if parts are infinite, a swift object could never overtake a slow one, because when the swift covers a part, the slow also covers a part (since there is no smallest part and no intervening rest). The slow is considered instead of the stationary object to avoid making speed irrelevant. The passage then clarifies that these three proofs are directed only against the claim that parts are infinite in every supposed extension and between every two extremities. If the opponent claims infinity only in the totality of extensions, then the proofs do not apply except by reductio on the finitude of the number of extensions.

Key Terms
امتناع وصول المتحرك
قطع نصف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the second proof claim about infinite parts of distance?
A) They make motion faster.
B) They require infinite time to traverse.
C) They are necessary for motion.
D) They are impossible to conceive.

Key Takeaway
The second proof shows that infinite parts of distance make it impossible to cover any finite distance in finite time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there goals in your life—spiritual, academic, or personal—that feel infinitely far because you only focus on the endless 'halfway points' of obstacles? How does this proof expose the self-deception of assuming progress requires an infinite chain of steps, when in reality Allah has made the path finite and traversable for the one who starts? Will you take the first step today, trusting in the finitude of His appointed distances, or will you remain stuck in the illusion of infinite halves?
?
This proof shows that an infinite series of divisions cannot be completed in finite time—yet you live your life as if tomorrow offers an infinite supply of moments to repent, grow closer to Allah, or fulfill responsibilities. How has the hidden assumption of an open-ended, infinitely divisible future deceived you into procrastinating on what you know you must do today? What one action will you take in the next hour to break that infinite regress of delay?
?
The argument relies on the logical necessity that if distance had infinite parts, motion would be impossible. But you observe motion every day—so you already accept that space must be finite. What if the same logic applies to your journey toward Allah? Are you treating repentance or good deeds as if they require an infinite series of perfect steps, when in fact the path is simple and finite? Will you let go of the paralyzing 'infinite halves' of perfectionism and simply move toward Him with what you have?

Third Proof: Overtaking Impossibility and Scope Clarification
Third proof and scope of the three arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third proof from the swift overtaking the slow, and the clarification about the scope of all three proofs.

Core Idea
If parts are infinite, swift can never overtake slow; and the proofs target a specific claim about infinite parts.

The third proof presents another paradox: a swift object cannot overtake a slow one if both move and parts are infinite, because when the swift covers a part, the slow also covers a part. The passage then clarifies that these proofs apply only to those who assert infinity of parts in every extension and between every two extremities, not to those who claim infinity only in the totality.

Guided Path
1
Read the third proof
Read the passage for the third proof. Understand why infinite parts prevent overtaking.
The argument uses no smallest part and no rest.
2
Understand the logic
Because each covers exactly one part simultaneously, the slow always stays ahead.
Speed becomes irrelevant.
3
Read the scope clarification
The author specifies that these proofs are effective only against a certain version of infinite parts.
Differentiate between infinity in every extension vs. in total.
4
Reflect on the distinction
Consider how this limits the refutation. The proofs do not apply to those who claim infinity in the sum total.
This nuance is important for proper understanding.

Source Text

The Fourth Proof: Ratio of Volumes Shows Finite Parts
A proof from ratio of volumes to finitude of parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the ratio of a finite volume to itself logically forces the finitude of its constituent parts.

Core Idea
If parts were infinite, a finite body's volume would have an impossible ratio.

This lesson unpacks the fourth proof from the text, a thought experiment that uses the relationship between volume and number of parts. By assuming a body formed from eight parts and then considering the ratio of its volume to its volume, the author demonstrates that the parts cannot be infinite. This is a pure rational argument, not dependent on measurement.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to get a general sense of the argument.
2
Understand the thought experiment
Notice that the proof begins by positing eight parts combined into a body with three dimensions. Why eight? To ensure it is a proper body.
The body is long, wide, deep, and divisible in the three dimensions.
3
Grasp the ratio comparison
The key move is comparing the ratio of volume to itself, which is linked to the ratio of parts to parts.
Volume is proportional to the number of parts.
4
See the contradiction
If parts were infinite, the ratio of a finite volume to itself would be like a finite number to infinite, which is impossible.
This is the core logical step.
5
Connect to finitude
Therefore, the parts must be finite. Reflect on how this proof avoids empirical measurement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : إنا نفرض اجتماع ثمانية من الأجزاء بحيث يصير المركب منها طويلاً، عريضاً عميقاً، منقسماً، فى الأقطار الثلاثة، متقاطعاً امتداداته على الزوايا القائمة، فبالضرورة يكون جسماً مع تناهي أجزائه، ثم إذا حاولنا بيان تناهي أجزاء كل جسم متناهي المقدار اعتبرنا نسبة حجمه إلى حجمه، فكانت نسبة متناه إلى متناه، لأن نسبة الحجم إلى الحجم نسبة الأجزاء إلى الأجزاء، إذ بحسبها يكون الحجم والمقدار ازدياداً، وانتقاصاً، فلو كانت الأجزاء غير متناهية، كانت نسبة المتناهي إلى المتناهي نسبة المتناهي إلى غير المتناهي، وهو محال .
Fourth: We posit the combination of eight parts such that the compound from them becomes long, wide, deep, divisible in the three dimensions, its extensions intersecting at right angles; then of necessity it is a body with finite parts. Then if we attempt to demonstrate the finitude of the parts of every body of finite magnitude, we consider the ratio of its volume to its volume: thus the ratio is of a finite to a finite, because the ratio of volume to volume is the ratio of parts to parts, since according to them volume and magnitude increase and decrease. If the parts were infinite, then the ratio of finite to finite would be the ratio of finite to infinite, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof for the finitude of parts. The proponent assumes eight parts combined to form a body that is long, wide, deep, divisible in three dimensions, with extensions intersecting at right angles. This body is necessarily finite in parts. Then, to prove that every body of finite magnitude has finite parts, he argues by taking the ratio of its volume to its own volume. Since the volume is finite, the ratio is finite to finite. But volume is proportional to the number of parts; so if parts were infinite, the ratio of a finite volume to itself would be the ratio of a finite number to an infinite number, which is impossible. Thus parts must be finite.

Key Terms
ثمانية أجزاء
نسبة الحجم
متناهي المقدار
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof requires empirical measurement of volumes.
Correction: It is a pure thought experiment based on the logical relation between volume and number of parts, not on actual measurement.

Checkpoint
Why does the fourth proof conclude that the parts must be finite?
A) Because eight parts always make a finite body.
B) Because the ratio of a finite volume to itself cannot equal the ratio of a finite to an infinite number.
C) Because infinite parts would make the body infinitely large.
D) Because extension cannot be divided into more than eight parts.

Key Takeaway
The ratio of a finite volume to itself logically requires the number of parts to be finite, because an infinite number would make the ratio impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof uses a simple thought experiment to establish a necessary truth about the physical world. Are there areas of your belief about God where you avoid using simple logical reasoning, preferring to remain in comfortable uncertainty? What would it cost you to apply the same rigorous thinking to your faith?
?
The argument hinges on the impossibility of a finite-to-finite ratio equaling a finite-to-infinite ratio. In your own life, do you ever try to make the finite (your efforts, time) equal the infinite (the weight of eternity) without relying on logic and revelation? How might this proof correct that tendency?
?
Consider the humility required to accept that something as basic as a body's volume leads to a logical conclusion about finitude. Are you willing to follow the reasoning wherever it leads, even if it challenges your assumptions about the world? What specific assumption do you need to re-examine today?

Fifth Proof and Interpenetration Response
Presents the fifth argument and the opponent's reply of interpenetration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth proof against infinite parts (the argument from volume increase) and the opponent's response of interpenetration.

Core Idea
Infinite parts would make every body infinitely large, but interpenetration blocks that conclusion.

This passage presents a key objection from the atomist to the theory of infinite parts, and a response: that interpenetration allows many parts to occupy the same space. Understanding this dialectic is crucial for assessing the plausibility of atomism.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof
Read the argument that if parts are infinite, every body would have infinite volume, which is absurd.
The proof assumes that volume is proportional to the number of parts.
2
Identify the interpenetration response
Notice the opponent claims that parts can interpenetrate, so increasing parts does not increase volume.
This response also aims to block the entailment about motion and time.
3
Reflect on the dialectic
Consider why this response is controversial and how an atomist might defend against it.
The passage does not refute the response; it leaves the debate open.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : أنه لو كان الحجم والمقدار بحسب الأجزاء، فلو كانت الأجزاء غير متناهية لزم في كل جسم أن يكون غير متناهي الحجم، واللازم ظاهر البطلان، والمشهور عن القائلين بلا تناهي الأجزاء في النفصي عن حديث زيادة الحجم ، ولحوق السريع البطيء أمران: أحدهما القول بالتداخل، وهو أن ينفذ أحد الجزئين في الآخر ويلاقيه بأسره، بحيث يصير حيزاهما واحداً، وحاصله منع زيادة الحجم بزيادة الأجزاء ، فلا يلزم من عدم تناهي الأجزاء أن يكون الحجم غير متناه ، ولا أن يكون بإزاء كل جزء من المسافة جزء من الحركة والزمان ليلزم عدم تناهيهما .
Fifth: If volume and magnitude are according to the parts, then if the parts were infinite, it would follow that every body is of infinite volume, and the consequent is obviously false. The famous [response] from the proponents of infinite parts regarding [the issue] of increase of volume and the overtaking of the swift by the slow are two things: one of them is the doctrine of interpenetration (al-tadākhul), which is that one part penetrates into the other and meets it entirely, such that their two positions become one. The upshot of this is to prevent the increase of volume by the increase of parts. So it does not follow from the infinity of parts that the volume is infinite, nor that for every part of the distance there is a part of motion and time, so as to entail their infinity.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof. The atomist argues that if volume and magnitude depend on the number of parts, then infinite parts would necessarily yield infinite volume for every body, which is absurd. However, the passage then notes that the proponents of infinite parts have a famous response consisting of two points. The first is the doctrine of interpenetration (al-tadākhul), which holds that one part can penetrate into another so that both occupy the same position, thereby preventing an increase in volume despite an increase in the number of parts. This response also aims to block the entailment that each part of distance corresponds to a part of motion and time, which would otherwise require infinite motion and time. The passage does not here refute this response but presents it as a counterargument that the atomist must address.

Key Terms
حجم
أجزاء
تداخل
زيادة الحجم
لحوق السريع بالبطيء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume this proof is decisive against infinite parts.
Correction: The passage shows that the proponents of infinite parts have a response (interpenetration), so the proof is not conclusive on its own.

Checkpoint
What is the 'doctrine of interpenetration' (al-tadākhul) meant to explain?
A) That parts can merge to form larger parts.
B) That multiple parts can occupy the same space without increasing volume.
C) That motion does not require time.
D) That body is composed of indivisible atoms.

Key Takeaway
The interpenetration doctrine is a response to the volume-increase argument, showing that infinite parts need not imply infinite volume.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been certain that an argument was conclusive, only to later discover a counter-response you had not considered? How does this passage challenge you to hold your intellectual conclusions with humility, even when they seem obvious?
?
When you encounter a counterargument that strikes you as far-fetched or impossible (like interpenetration), do you dismiss it outright, or do you try to understand its logical role in the debate? What does your reaction reveal about your willingness to engage with opposing viewpoints?
?
This lesson shows that even a seemingly absurd proposal (two parts occupying the same space) can be used to block a logical entailment. Are there areas in your own beliefs where you have rejected a possibility too quickly because it seemed implausible, rather than honestly evaluating its logical merit? What would it take for you to reconsider?

Objection and Answer: Atoms as Individuals
Presents an objection by al-Nazzam and the atomist reply.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the atomist reply refutes al-Nazzam's claim that bodies consist of infinite atoms by focusing on a finite number of parts.

Core Idea
Finite parts prove finitude, even if infinite atoms exist.

This passage presents a key objection from the theologian al-Nazzam against the atomist position. He argues that indivisible atoms cannot exist alone and that every body must be composed of infinite atoms. The atomist reply cleverly narrows the discussion to a finite subset of parts, showing that the finitude of a body can be established without addressing the totality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the structure: 'If it is said... We reply...'
2
Identify the objection
What is al-Nazzam's claim about atoms? He says atoms cannot exist in isolation, only within bodies, and bodies have infinite atoms.
3
Understand the reply
The reply (qulnā) suggests restricting the argument to eight parts. How does this refute the objection? By focusing on a finite sample, the infinite regress is avoided.
4
Reflect on the significance
This shows a strategy of 'bracketing' the infinite to prove finiteness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : مذهب النظام أن الجوهر الفرد يمتنع وجوده على الانفراد، وإنما يكون في ضمن الجسم، وكل جسم، فمن جواهر غير متناهية . قلنا نفرض الكلام في ثمانية أجزاء من الجسم.
If it is said: The doctrine of al-Nazzam is that the indivisible substance (al-jawhar al-fard) is impossible to exist in isolation, but only within a body, and every body consists of infinite substances. We reply: We posit the discussion concerning eight parts of the body.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objector states that according to al-Nazzām, the indivisible atom cannot exist independently; it only exists within a body, and every body is composed of infinite such atoms. This would seem to support the position of infinite parts. The answer (qulnā) is that we may restrict our argument to eight specific parts of the body. By narrowing the discussion to a finite, small number of parts, the issue of infinity is bypassed; the finitude of those eight parts is sufficient to demonstrate that the body in question is finite in parts, regardless of whether the body as a whole is thought to be composed of infinite atoms. This reply refutes the objection by shifting the focus from the totality to a concrete finite sample.

Key Terms
جوهر فرد
انفراد
نظام
ثمانية أجزاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Nazzam's objection proves that bodies must have infinite parts.
Correction: The atomist reply shows that by focusing on a finite subset, the finitude of a body can still be maintained.

Checkpoint
How does the atomist reply to the claim that every body has infinite atoms?
A) By denying that atoms can exist alone.
B) By assuming that atoms are extended.
C) By restricting the argument to eight parts.
D) By accepting infinite atoms but denying infinite size.

Key Takeaway
The atomist answer refutes al-Nazzam's objection by limiting the discussion to a finite number of body parts, thereby proving finitude without addressing the whole.

?
The atomist reply did not answer every aspect of the objection but still provided a valid proof of finitude. Are you willing to accept limited but solid evidences in matters of faith, or do you demand absolute completeness before you submit? What does your answer reveal about your heart?

The Fourth Argument for the Finitude of Parts
Fourth argument uses ratio of volume to parts to prove finitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth kalam argument for the finitude of parts, which uses the ratio of volumes to prove that infinite parts lead to an impossible ratio.

Core Idea
A finite body cannot have infinite parts, because its volume ratio would be contradictory.

This passage presents a nuanced argument that finite bodies must have finite parts. The author sets up a constructed body from eight parts and then examines the ratio of its volume to itself. Because volume corresponds directly to number of parts, the ratio of finite volumes would have to be a ratio of finite to infinite if parts were infinite—an impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Visualize the eight-part model
Understand the constructed composite from eight parts arranged in three dimensions, forming a finite body with length, width, and depth.
This is a thought experiment to establish a baseline finite body.
2
Grasp the ratio argument
Recognize that the ratio of a body's volume to itself is a finite-to-finite ratio, and that volume ratio equals the ratio of the number of parts.
Because volume increases or decreases with the number of parts.
3
Identify the contradiction
If parts were infinite, the ratio of the body's volume to itself would become finite-to-infinite, which is impossible. Therefore, the parts must be finite.
The argument is a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : إنا نفرض اجتماع ثمانية من الأجزاء بحيث يصير المركب منها طويلاً، عريضاً عميقاً، منقسماً، فى الأقطار الثلاثة، متقاطعاً امتداداته على الزوايا القائمة، فبالضرورة يكون جسماً مع تناهي أجزائه، ثم إذا حاولنا بيان تناهي أجزاء كل جسم متناهي المقدار اعتبرنا نسبة حجمه إلى حجمه، فكانت نسبة متناه إلى متناه، لأن نسبة الحجم إلى الحجم نسبة الأجزاء إلى الأجزاء، إذ بحسبها يكون الحجم والمقدار ازدياداً، وانتقاصاً، فلو كانت الأجزاء غير متناهية، كانت نسبة المتناهي إلى المتناهي نسبة المتناهي إلى غير المتناهي، وهو محال .
The fourth: We assume a composition of eight parts such that the composite becomes long, wide, deep, divisible in the three dimensions, with its extensions intersecting at right angles. Necessarily it is a body with finite parts. Then if we attempt to demonstrate the finitude of parts of every body of finite magnitude, we consider the ratio of its volume to its volume; so it is a ratio of finite to finite, because the ratio of volume to volume is the ratio of parts to parts, since by them volume and magnitude increase and decrease. If the parts were infinite, then the ratio of the finite to the finite would be the ratio of the finite to the infinite, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth argument for the finitude of parts in a body. The author begins by assuming a composition of eight parts arranged in three dimensions, forming a finite body. Then he states that to prove all finite bodies have finite parts, we consider the ratio of volume to volume. Since volume corresponds to number of parts, the ratio of volumes is the ratio of parts. For a finite body, the ratio of its volume to another finite volume is a ratio of finite to finite. If parts were infinite, then the ratio of a finite volume to a finite volume would involve a finite to infinite ratio, which is impossible. Thus parts must be finite. The argument relies on the correspondence between volume and number of parts.

Key Terms
جزء (part)
متناهي (finite)
غير متناهي (infinite)
نسبة (ratio)
جسم (body)
حجم (volume)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the argument assumes infinite parts in a finite body; it actually shows the impossibility of that scenario.
Correction: The argument is a reductio: assuming infinite parts leads to a contradiction in ratios, so the assumption is false.

Checkpoint

A) Finite to finite
B) Finite to infinite
C) Infinite to infinite
D) Impossible to determine

Key Takeaway
The fourth argument proves that any finite body must have a finite number of parts, because if parts were infinite, the ratio of its volume to itself would be an impossible ratio of finite to infinite.

?
If this argument is sound, then every physical thing you encounter has a finite structure. How does that change the way you value or attach to material things? Are you ready to accept that your own body, despite its complexity, is finite and dependent, and that your ultimate hope lies beyond the physical?

The Fifth Argument: Refuting Interpenetration and Leap
Fifth argument against infinite parts with refutation of tadakhul and tafrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth argument against infinite parts and why the doctrines of interpenetration (tadakhul) and leap (tafrah) are rationally and empirically false.

Core Idea
Infinite parts would require infinite volume, and interpenetration/leap cannot salvage it.

The author presents a powerful argument: if volume depends on number of parts, then infinite parts would mean infinite volume for every body, which is absurd. Defenders of infinite parts propose interpenetration (parts occupy same space) and leap (moving without traversing intermediate points) to avoid the consequence. This lesson examines the argument and shows why both counter-claims fail.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Pay attention to the logical structure: argument, two counter-claims, refutation.
Note that the author calls both counter-claims false by necessity.
2
Understand the fifth argument
What is the premise and why does it lead to infinite volume?
The conclusion that infinite parts lead to infinite volume is deemed absurd.
3
Compare tadakhul and tafrah
How do they attempt to avoid the conclusion? Tadakhul says parts merge, tafrah says mover skips points.
4
Grasp the refutations
Why is tadakhul false? Because it implies whole equals part. Why is tafrah false? Because it implies cutting a distance without motion.
There is also a sensory proof: drawing a pen yields a continuous line, not a dotted one.
5
Reflect on the implications
Why does this strengthen the case against infinite parts?
The failure of these counter-claims reinforces the original argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : أنه لو كان الحجم والمقدار بحسب الأجزاء، فلو كانت الأجزاء غير متناهية لزم في كل جسم أن يكون غير متناهي الحجم، واللازم ظاهر البطلان، والمشهور عن القائلين بلا تناهي الأجزاء في النفصي عن حديث زيادة الحجم ، ولحوق السريع البطيء أمران: أحدهما القول بالتداخل، وهو أن ينفذ أحد الجزئين في الآخر ويلاقيه بأسره، بحيث يصير حيزاهما واحداً، وحاصله منع زيادة الحجم بزيادة الأجزاء ، فلا يلزم من عدم تناهي الأجزاء أن يكون الحجم غير متناه ، ولا أن يكون بإزاء كل جزء من المسافة جزء من الحركة والزمان ليلزم عدم تناهيهما . وثانيهما: القول بالطفرة ، وهو أن يترك المتحرك حداً من المسافة، ويحصل في حد آخر من غير محاذاة وملاقاة لما بينهما، وحاصله قطع بعض حدود المسافة من غير ملاقاة لأجزائه وحينئذ لا يلزم امتناع أن يصل المتحرك إلى غاية ما أو يلحق السريع البطيء، وكلا الأمرين باطل بالضرورة. أما التداخل فلان حاصله تساوي الكل والجزء في العظم ، وأما الطفرة فلأن معناها يؤول إلى قطع مسافة ما، من غير حركة فيها، وقطع أجزائها، ومن الشواهد الحسية لبطلانها أنا نمد القلم فيحصل خط أسود من غير أن يبقى في خلاله أجزاء بيض، وليس ذلك لفرط اختلاط الأجزاء البيض بالسود، بحيث لا تترك الآن أجزاء بيض لا تترك الإحساس بالبيض، بل لا نسبة لها إليها؛ لكونها غير متناهية، فينبغي أن يقع الإحساس بالبيض ، وقد يستدل على نفي التداخل بأنه إن كان بالأسر بمعنى أن يلاقي الجزء بكليته الجزء الآخر بحيث يصير حيزاهما واحداً لم يكن الوسطاني حاجباً للطرفين عن التماس ، وبقي الإشكال بالنظر إلى الأجزاء المتماسة، بل لو وقع ذلك في جميع الأجزاء لم يحصل هناك تأليف، وامتداد في الجهات، فلم يحصل الجسم، وإن كان لا بالأسر، وذلك بأن يلاقي الجزء الجزء، ويداخله بشيء دون شيء لزم التجزيء، ولو بالفرض مع بقاء الإشكال بحاله.
The fifth: If volume and magnitude are according to parts, then if parts were infinite, it would follow that every body has infinite volume, and the consequence is clearly false. The famous response from those who affirm infinite parts regarding the refutation of the increase of volume and the overtaking of fast and slow [in motion] are two things: One is the doctrine of interpenetration (tadakhul), which is that one part penetrates the other and meets it entirely, so that their two loci become one. Its gist is to deny the increase of volume by increase of parts. So from the infinity of parts it does not necessarily follow that volume is infinite, nor that for every part of the distance there is a part of motion and time, leading to their infinity. The second is the doctrine of the leap (tafrah), which is that the mover leaves one limit of the distance and arrives at another limit without being opposite or meeting what is between them. Its gist is that it cuts some limits of the distance without meeting its parts. Then it does not necessarily follow the impossibility of the mover reaching an endpoint or the fast overtaking the slow. Both matters are false by necessity. As for interpenetration, because its gist is the equality of the whole and the part in size. As for the leap, because its meaning amounts to cutting a distance without motion in it and without cutting its parts. Among the sensory proofs of its falsity is that we extend a pen and a black line arises without white parts remaining in between. That is not due to excessive mixing of white parts with black so that they are not distinguished by sensation, because the sensible parts are much fewer than the separated [?] ones, rather, there is no ratio of them to them because they are infinite; thus sensation of white should occur. And one can argue against interpenetration by saying that if it is total, meaning that the part meets the other part entirely so that their two loci become one, then the middle would not be a barrier to the contact of the two ends, and the problem remains with regard to the contiguous parts. Indeed, if that occurred in all parts, no composition would result, nor extension in dimensions, so the body would not result. And if it is not total, that is, the part meets the part and enters into it by some amount without the other, then division would be entailed, even if only by assumption, while the problem remains as it is.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth argument against infinite parts, along with the refutation of two counter-theories: interpenetration (tadakhul) and leap (tafrah). The argument states that if volume depends on number of parts, then infinite parts would mean infinite volume, which is absurd. Those who defend infinite parts propose tadakhul (parts interpenetrating so volume doesn't increase) and tafrah (mover leaps over intermediate points so motion doesn't require infinite steps). The author then refutes both by necessity. Tadakhul is false because it implies whole equals part in size. Tafrah is false because it amounts to moving without moving. A sensory proof: drawing a pen yields a continuous black line with no white gaps; if tafrah occurred, there would be gaps. Also a logical refutation of tadakhul: if total interpenetration, middle parts wouldn't block contact; if partial, the part would be divisible. Both lead to contradictions.

Key Terms

طفرة
حجم
جزء
حركة
مسافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Interpenetration (tadakhul) and leap (tafrah) are valid ways to avoid the consequence of infinite volume in a body with infinite parts.
Correction: Both are false by necessity; tadakhul implies whole equals part, and tafrah implies moving without motion; sensory proof of continuous line contradicts tafrah.

Checkpoint

A) A moving object cannot change direction
B) When a pen is drawn, a continuous black line appears without gaps
C) The sun appears to move across the sky
D) Two objects cannot occupy the same space

Key Takeaway
The fifth argument shows infinite parts lead to absurd conclusions, and the attempted rescues of interpenetration and leap are both rationally and empirically untenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The pen line proves that reality does not allow gaps where we imagine them. Where have you been expecting a 'leap' in your spiritual growth—skipping the slow, steady effort of worship and obedience? What specific step will you take today to traverse the distance rather than leap?
?
If tadakhul makes the whole equal to a part, what 'whole' in your life (your time, your devotion, your character) have you been treating as if it can be achieved without proportional input from its parts? What is one part you have neglected that needs attention now?

Answer to the Infinite Divisibility Objection
Taftazani answers the objection that traversing a distance requires infinite time due to infinite divisibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Taftazani defends the possibility of traversing a finite distance in finite time despite infinite divisibility by appealing to the mutual divisibility of time and motion.

Core Idea
Infinite divisibility does not require infinite time because time is also infinitely divisible.

This passage tackles a classic objection: if a finite distance is infinitely divisible, how can it be traversed in a finite time? Taftazani presents the standard answer that time itself is infinitely divisible, so the infinite parts of motion correspond to infinite parts of time. But he also addresses a subtle counter-objection that this answer is circular, and clarifies why it stands.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Get the overall flow of the argument.
Notice the dialectical structure: problem, answer, objection, reply.
2
Identify the objection and the answer
The objection: traversing a finite distance requires traversing infinite half-distances, so infinite time is needed. The answer: time is also infinitely divisible, so the infinite parts correspond.
3
Understand the counter-objection
The counter says this is not a real proof but just another argument (the 'confined between two confines' argument).
See how the objection shifts the ground.
4
Analyze the final response
Taftazani acknowledges the point but asserts that for longitudinal extension (motion, time) the point is clear enough to clarify the case of the body.
This shows the elegance of the response.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this resolves Zeno's paradox of the arrow or dichotomy, and why it's important for kalam arguments about motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وقطع ما لا يتناهى فيما يتناهى شلال) قد يجاب عن إشكال قطع المسافة المعينة بأنه إنما يتوقف على زمان غير متناهي الأجزاء ينطبق كل جزء منه على جزء من الحركة، وهو على جزء من المسافة، وهذا لا يستلزم عدم تناهي الزمان، لأن المحدود من الحركة والزمان يشتمل على أجزاء غير متناهية، كالجسم المتناهي، وهذا كما أن المسافة المعينة تحتمل عند الفلاسفة الانقسام إلى غير النهاية، ولا يمتنع قطعها في زمان متناه أن قطعها يتوقف على قطع نصفها ونصف نصفها ، وهلم جرا إلى ما لا يتناهى وذلك لأن كلا من الحركة والزمان المحدودين أيضاً قابل للانقسام إلى غير النهاية ، ويدفع بأن ما يوجد شيئاً فشيئاً من بداية إلى نهاية، فامتناع كونه غير متناهي العدد معلوم بالضرورة، والقول به ضلال عن طريق الحق، بخلاف قبوله الانقسام إلى غير النهاية بالمعنى الذي ذكروه على ما مرّ. فإن قيل : هذا ليس تمشية البرهان قطع المسافة، بل رجوعاً إلى برهان المحصور بين حاصرين. قلنا : نعم إلا أن هذا لما كان فيما له امتداد طولي فقط كالحركة والزمان في غاية الظهور بين به حال الجسم.
He said: 'And cutting what does not end in what ends [shalal?].' It may be answered concerning the problem of cutting a specific distance: that it depends on a time with infinite parts, each part of which corresponds to a part of the motion, and it corresponds to a part of the distance. And this does not entail the infinity of time, because the finite [portion] of motion and time contains infinite parts, like the finite body. And this is just as the specific distance admits according to the philosophers division to infinity, and it is not impossible to traverse it in finite time, because traversing it depends on traversing its half, and half of its half, and so on to infinity. That is because both the finite motion and time are also divisible to infinity. And it is repelled by [the fact] that what exists bit by bit from beginning to end, the impossibility of it being infinite in number is known by necessity, and saying so is straying from the path of truth, unlike its accepting division to infinity in the sense they mentioned as has passed. If it is said: 'This is not a smooth running of the proof of traversing distance, but rather a return to the proof of the confined between two confines.' We say: Yes, except that this, since it concerns what has only longitudinal extension like motion and time, is in utmost clarity to clarify the state of the body.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents an answer to the classic objection that traversing a finite distance would require infinite time because the distance is infinitely divisible. The response is that time itself is also infinitely divisible, so the infinite parts of motion and time correspond to the infinite parts of the distance. The argument then faces a counter-objection: this is not actually a proof of traversing distance but a different argument (the proof of the 'confined between two confines'). The reply acknowledges this but notes that in the case of longitudinal extension (like motion and time), the point is so clear that it clarifies the state of the body as well.

Key Terms
قطع المسافة
زمان
حركة
انقسام
لا يتناهى
محصور بين حاصرين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The problem of infinite divisibility is solved by denying that the distance is infinitely divisible.
Correction: The solution acknowledges infinite divisibility but argues that time and motion share the same property, so the infinite parts are only potential, not actual.

Checkpoint
How does the response defend the possibility of traversing a finite distance in finite time?
A) By denying that a finite distance is infinitely divisible.
B) By distinguishing between actual and potential infinity.
C) By noting that time is also infinitely divisible, allowing correspondence of infinite parts.
D) By appealing to God's power to collapse the distance.

Key Takeaway
The problem of infinite divisibility is resolved not by rejecting division but by recognizing that time and motion share the same property of potential infinite divisibility, so no actual infinity is required.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The objection of infinite divisibility is often used to deny accountability—since we never truly 'arrive' at the end of a task. But Taftazani shows the absurdity of that argument. In what area of your life are you using such an excuse to delay obedience to Allah? What step will you take today to prove that argument wrong?
?
If time and motion share the property of infinite divisibility, then nothing stops you from beginning a good deed now. What one small action will you take today, knowing that it is not hindered by the fallacy of infinite steps? How will you ensure that you actually start?

First Philosophical Proof Against the Indivisible Atom
Taftazani states the first way the philosophers deny the indivisible atom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first philosophical argument against the existence of the indivisible atom, based on directionality.

Core Idea
Directionality in an atom implies parts, so it cannot be indivisible.

The philosophers argue against the atomists' concept of an indivisible particle by showing that even the most basic spatial property—direction—forces us to admit division. Taftazani presents this as the first of their proofs, challenging the very foundation of atomic theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to see the concise form of the argument.
Notice the compressed style of the proof.
2
Understand the premise
The argument starts from the idea that an atom has two different directions (e.g., left and right).
The term 'جهة' (direction) is key.
3
Follow the conclusion
Because the part toward one direction is distinct from that toward another, the atom must have parts and thus is divisible.
This directly negates indivisibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طرق نفي الجوهر الفرد عند الفلاسفة قال (وأما الفلاسفة) فلهم في نفي الجوهر الفرد طرق منها : الأول: أن ما منه إلى جهة غير ما منه إلى جهة أخرى فينقسم .
Ways of denying the indivisible atom according to the philosophers. He said: 'As for the philosophers, they have ways of denying the indivisible atom, among them: The first: That that from which there is a direction is other than that from which there is another direction, so it divides.'
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage introduces a philosophical argument against the existence of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). The first proof is based on directionality: if we consider a minimal point (atom) and suppose it has two different directions (like right and left, or up and down), then that which leads to one direction must be distinct from that which leads to the other direction. This implies that the atom has distinguishable parts, and therefore it is divisible. This is a classic argument from geometry: any extended entity must have parts; an indivisible point cannot have spatial dimensions.

Key Terms
جوهر فرد
نفي
طرق
جهة
انقسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument assumes the atom has physical extension.
Correction: The argument shows that even conceptually, directionality implies parts, regardless of physical size.

Checkpoint
According to the first philosophical proof against the indivisible atom, what indicates that an atom must be divisible?
A) It has weight.
B) It has two opposite directions.
C) It is created in time.
D) It is composed of smaller particles.

Key Takeaway
The first philosophical proof against the indivisible atom uses directionality to show that any spatial point must have distinct parts, thus it is divisible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often trust your senses and intuitions about reality. But this simple argument shows that reason can overturn what seems obvious. Is there an area of your faith or worldview where you have been relying on intuition rather than careful reasoning? Will you examine it honestly today?
?
The atomists held a view that seemed plausible until a clear logical proof refuted it. What is a belief you hold that you have never critically examined? Are you willing to subject it to the same logical scrutiny, even if it is uncomfortable?

Answering the Objection on Infinite Divisibility and Finite Motion
Answering the objection about traversing an infinitely divisible finite distance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how kalam scholars argue that traversing an infinitely divisible finite distance does not require infinite time, because motion and time are themselves infinitely divisible.

Core Idea
Infinite divisibility of distance does not imply infinite time for traversal.

This passage addresses a classic objection against the possibility of motion: if a distance is infinitely divisible, how can it be traversed in finite time? The answer lies in the parallel infinite divisibility of motion and time themselves. Al-Sanusi presents an objection, a response, a further objection, and a clarification, showing the coherence of the rational argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main objection
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation. Focus on the opening objection: that cutting a finite distance requires infinite time because of infinite half-distances.
The objection is attributed to philosophers who hold to infinite divisibility.
2
Understand the answer: motion and time are also infinitely divisible
The response states that finite motion and time themselves contain infinite parts, so each part of motion corresponds to a part of time, allowing traversal in finite time.
This is the core move: the same divisibility applies to all three.
3
Note the further objection about the proof type
A second objection says this response is not running the original proof but retreating to the 'confined between two confiners' argument.
This is a metatargument about the nature of the proof.
4
See the response: it's acceptable in this case
Al-Sanusi concedes the point but says that because motion and time have only longitudinal extension, the argument is extremely clear and suffices to show the point.
The clarification shows the argument is valid for this specific context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وقطع ما لا يتناهى فيما يتناهى شلال) مع قد يجاب عن إشكال قطع المسافة المعينة بأنه إنما يتوقف على زمان غير متناهي الأجزاء ينطبق كل جزء منه على جزء من الحركة، وهو على جزء من المسافة، وهذا لا يستلزم عدم تناهي الزمان، لأن المحدود من الحركة والزمان يشتمل على أجزاء غير متناهية، كالجسم المتناهي، وهذا كما أن المسافة المعينة تحتمل عند الفلاسفة الانقسام إلى غير النهاية، ولا يمتنع قطعها في زمان متناه أن قطعها يتوقف على قطع نصفها ونصف نصفها ، وهلم جرا إلى ما لا يتناهى وذلك لأن كلا من الحركة والزمان المحدودين أيضاً قابل للانقسام إلى غير النهاية ، ويدفع بأن ما يوجد شيئاً فشيئاً من بداية إلى نهاية، فامتناع كونه غير متناهي العدد معلوم بالضرورة، والقول به ضلال عن طريق الحق، بخلاف قبوله الانقسام إلى غير النهاية بالمعنى الذي ذكروه على ما مرّ. فإن قيل : هذا ليس تمشية (۱) البرهان قطع المسافة، بل رجوعاً إلى برهان المحصور بين حاصرين. قلنا : نعم إلا أن هذا لما كان فيما له امتداد طولي فقط كالحركة والزمان في غاية الظهور بين به حال الجسم.
He said: And cutting what is infinite in what is finite [؟] fall [؟] with. It may be answered about the problem of cutting a specific distance that it only depends on a time infinite in parts, each part of which corresponds to a part of motion, and it corresponds to a part of distance, and this does not entail infinity of time, because the limited motion and time contain infinite parts, like the finite body. And this is like how a specific distance, according to the philosophers, admits division to infinity, and it is not impossible to cut it in finite time, but cutting it depends on cutting its half and half of its half, and so on to infinity, because both the limited motion and time are also divisible to infinity. And it is refuted that what exists little by little from beginning to end, the impossibility of its being infinite in number is necessarily known, and saying so is deviation from the path of truth, unlike its admitting division to infinity in the sense they mentioned as previously. If it is said: This is not a running of the proof of cutting the distance, but a return to the proof of the confined between two confiners. We say: Yes, except that this, since it is in what has only longitudinal extension like motion and time, is extremely clear, by it the state of the body is shown.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer concerning the problem of traversing an infinitely divisible finite distance. The objection states that cutting a finite distance requires infinite time because it involves traversing an infinite number of half-distances. The answer begins by noting that finite time and finite motion themselves are also infinitely divisible, just like the distance. Therefore, the infinite divisibility of the distance does not necessitate infinite time, because each part of motion corresponds to a part of time, both being simultaneously divisible. Then a further objection is raised: this response does not actually run the proof of cutting the distance but retreats to the proof of the 'confined between two confiners' (a different argument). The answer concedes this but notes that since the case involves only longitudinal extension (like motion and time), the argument is extremely clear, and by it the state of the body is shown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That infinite divisibility of a finite distance necessarily requires infinite time to traverse it.
Correction: Finite motion and finite time are also infinitely divisible, so each part of motion corresponds to a part of time, allowing traversal in finite time.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The infinite divisibility of space does not thwart finite motion because motion and time are equally divisible, and the argument holds especially for longitudinal extension.

?

?

Five Philosophical Proofs Against the Indivisible Atom
Listing five philosophical arguments against the indivisible atom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand five philosophical arguments used to reject the existence of an indivisible atom.

Core Idea
Philosophers argue that atoms must have parts because they have direction, contact, and motion.

This passage presents five distinct methods (turūq) that philosophers employ to disprove the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). Each proof targets a different aspect — direction, combination, stacking, illumination, and movement — to show that atoms must be divisible. As you read, notice how each proof reduces the alleged atom to something that must have distinct parts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overall sense of the five proofs. Don't worry about details yet.
The passage lists five arguments; notice the use of 'الأول', 'الثاني', etc.
2
Identify each proof's scenario
For each proof, identify the key physical scenario (e.g., joining two parts, stacking three parts) and the logical conclusion drawn.
Each proof uses a different scenario to argue for divisibility.
3
Understand the reasoning
Focus on the logical structure: how does the scenario force the atom to have parts? For instance, the first proof notes that different directions imply distinct parts.
4
Reflect on the philosophical goal
Consider why these arguments are important for the philosophers' rejection of atomism. They aim to show that the concept of an indivisible atom leads to contradictions.
These arguments are part of a larger debate between philosophers and theologians.
5
Connect to broader context
Think about how these proofs relate to other arguments in kalam and philosophy. For example, the first proof is similar to arguments against point-like entities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال (وأما الفلاسفة) فلهم في نفي الجوهر الفرد طرق منها : الأول: أن ما منه إلى جهة غير ما منه إلى جهة أخرى فينقسم . الثاني : : إذا انضم جزء إلى جزء فإما أن يلاقيه بالأسر فلا حجم، فلا مقدار أو لا بالأسر فيلزم الانقسام. الثالث : إذا تراصت ثلاثة أجزاء فالوسط إن منع الطرفين من التلاقي انقسم، وإلا فلا حجم . الرابع : أنه إذا أشرقت الشمس على صفحة من الأجزاء، فالوجه المضيء المقابل غير الآخر. الخامس : إذا وقع جزء على ملتقى جزءين انقسمت الثلاث وذلك بأن يفرض عليه أو يتحرك من جزء إلى آخر، فكونه متحركاً إنما يكون عند الملتقى، أو يفرض خط من أربعة أجزاء فوق الأول جزء، وتحت الرابع جزء، ثم تحركا معاً على السواء، فالتحاذي يكون على الملتقى، أو يفرض خط من خمسة، فوق كل طرف جزء، فيتحركا حتى التقيا فالثالث يكون على ملتقاهما ] .
He said: And as for the philosophers, they have methods for negating the indivisible atom. Among them: First: That that from which to one direction is not that from which to another direction, so it divides. Second: If a part is joined to a part, then either it contacts it completely so there is no size, no magnitude, or not completely, so division follows. Third: If three parts are stacked, then the middle one, if it prevents the two ends from meeting, divides; otherwise, no size. Fourth: If the sun shines on a surface of parts, then the illuminated face is other than the other. Fifth: If a part falls on the meeting point of two parts, the three divide, and that is by assuming upon it, or moving from part to another, so its being moving is only at the meeting point; or by assuming a line of four parts, above the first part and below the fourth part, then both move equally, so alignment is at the meeting point; or by assuming a line of five parts, above each end a part, they move until they meet, so the third is at their meeting point.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of five methods (turūq) used by the philosophers to deny the existence of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). Each method is briefly described. The first method: since an atom would have multiple directions (right, left, etc.), those directions are distinct, so the atom must have parts. The second method: if two parts are joined, either they completely coincide resulting in no increase in size, or they do not completely coincide, implying that they have parts and thus division. The third method: if three parts are stacked, the middle one either prevents the ends from touching, in which case it is divisible, or it does not, in which case its size is null. The fourth method: when sunlight falls on a surface of atoms, the illuminated face is different from the rest, implying distinct parts. The fifth method: various scenarios involving movement and meeting points show that atoms would have to divide at meeting points.

Key Terms
الجوهر الفرد
نفي
طرق
القسمة
الانضمام
التراص
إشراق الشمس
ملتقى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The first
B) The second
C) The third
D) The fourth

Key Takeaway
Philosophers use five distinct physical scenarios to demonstrate that the concept of an indivisible atom leads to contradictions, forcing the atom to be divisible.

The First Two Proofs Against the Indivisible Atom
Explaining the foundation and first two arguments against the indivisible atom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical arguments that show an indivisible atom cannot exist because it would have multiple directions (first proof) and because joining two such atoms leads to a contradiction (second proof).

Core Idea
Indivisible atoms can't exist because they'd have directions and joining them leads to absurdity.

The author begins by noting that the many proofs against the indivisible atom reduce to a few foundational principles. He then presents two of these principles, each showing a logical flaw in the concept of an indivisible substance. The first argument uses the necessary multiplicity of directions, the second explores the implications of joining two atoms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall flow. Notice how the author first sets up the classification of proofs, then gives two specific arguments.
The second proof is incomplete in this passage; it ends mid-sentence.
2
Understand the first proof
Focus on the first proof: if an indivisible atom exists, it would have directions (right, left, etc.). Since these directions are distinct, the atom must have parts, contradicting indivisibility.
This proof shows that even a simple substance cannot be free of spatial differentiation.
3
Understand the second proof
Examine the second proof: if two atoms join, either they touch completely (no increase in space) which yields no volume, or they don't touch completely (implies parts). Both options create a contradiction.
The argument relies on the idea that composition must produce magnitude.
4
Reflect on the underlying principle
Consider why both proofs share the common theme: they derive a contradiction from the assumption of an indivisible part, showing that division is necessary.
These are just two of several 'methods' (طرق) the author alludes to.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يريد أن أدلة نفي الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ على كثرتها ترجع إلى عدة أصول، يتفرع على كل منها وجوه من الاستدلال فجعلت بمنزلة الطرق، وأشير في عنوان كل منها إلى وجه الضعف، ومورد المنع ، فمنها ما يبتنى على أن تعدد جهات الشيء ونهاياته تستلزم الانقسام في ذاته، وهي وجوه : الأول : أنه لو وجد الجزء أي الجوهر المتميز الذي لا انقسام فيه أصلاً لتعددت جهاته ضرورة فتتعدد جوانبه وأطرافه، لأن ما منه إلى اليمين غير ما منه إلى اليسار وكذا الفوق والتحت والقدام والخلف فيلزم انقسامه على تقدير عدم انقسامه محال . وهو الثاني: أنه إذا انضم جزء إلى جزء، فإما أن يلاقيه بالكلية بحيث لا يزيد حيز الجزئين على حيز الواحد فيلزم أن لا يحصل من انضمام الأجزاء حجم ومقدار،
He intends that the proofs for negating the indivisible part (which does not divide), despite their multiplicity, go back to several foundations, branching from each are aspects of inference, so they are made as methods, and in the title of each is indicated the point of weakness and point of prevention. Among them are those based on that the multiplicity of directions and extremities of a thing entails division in itself, and they are aspects: First: That if the part exists, i.e., the distinct substance that has absolutely no division, then its directions would necessarily multiply, so its sides and extremities multiply, because that from which to the right is not that from which to the left, and likewise above, below, front, and back, so its division follows; on the assumption of its non-division it is impossible. That is the first. Second: That if a part is joined to a part, then either it contacts it entirely such that the space of the two parts does not exceed the space of one, then no volume or magnitude would result from joining parts,
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage explains that the multitude of proofs against the indivisible atom trace back to a few foundational principles. The author then details the first two proofs based on the principle of multiplicity of directions and the principle of joining. The first proof: if an indivisible atom existed, it would necessarily have multiple directions (right, left, up, down, front, back). Since these directions are distinct, the atom must have parts, contradicting its indivisibility. The second proof: if two atoms are joined, either they touch completely so that the combined space does not exceed the space of one, which would mean no magnitude results from composition, or they do not touch completely, which implies they have parts and thus division. The text breaks off during the second proof.

Key Terms
الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ
تعدد الجهات
الانضمام
حجم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That an indivisible atom could be dimensionless and have no spatial extension.
Correction: The first proof shows that any existing thing in space must have distinguishable directions, which imply parts; thus an indivisible atom cannot be dimensionless without contradiction.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what does the multiplicity of directions imply about the indivisible atom?
A) It is point-like
B) It must have volume
C) It must have parts
D) It cannot exist

Key Takeaway
The first two proofs show that an indivisible atom would logically require parts either through its inherent directions or through the implications of joining with another atom.

?

Which relationships in your life are stagnant because you insist on full contact without compromise?
